          UPON hearing the counsel the Court made the following
                             O R D E R
Delhi
1. Ms. Swati Ghidiyal, learned counsel appearing for the GNCT of Delhi,
seeks and is granted time till 27 th July, 2026 to file a response to I.A.
No.223523/2025.
2. Rejoinder thereto be filed by a week thereafter.
3. Mr.  Rahul  Kaushik,  learned  senior  counsel  appearing  for  455
contractual  teachers,  places  before  us  a  detailed  note.  Inter  alia,  it
appears  therefrom  that  in  2020,  200  contractual  teachers  were
appointed/engaged  by  the  GNCT  of  Delhi.  This  position  is  vehemently
disputed by Ms. Ghildiyal, learned counsel for GNCT of Delhi.
4. We are a little surprised that in 2020, when COVID was at its peak,
the country was in severe crisis and oxygen was available at a premium,
200 contractual teachers could be appointed by the GNCT of Delhi for
educating special children. A serious doubt is created in our mind in regard
to the correctness of the facts appearing in the detailed note placed by Mr.
13

--- Page 22 ---
Kaushik.
5. Without expressing any final opinion on the claims as raised, we
require the contractual teachers represented by Mr. Kaushik to file an
affidavit bringing on record all the appointment/engagement letters issued
to them. The affidavit must further disclose whether any of the petitioners
in SLP (C) No.16838 of 2025 has participated in the recruitment processes
initiated in the years 2022 and 2023. These petitioners shall also indicate
the  category  to  which  they  belong,  viz.  PGT,  TGT,  PRT  or  any  other
category. 
6. Let such affidavit be filed by two weeks from date with copy to the
advocate-on-record for the GNCT of Delhi.
7. On receipt of such affidavit, the  GNCT of  Delhi may file  a reply
affidavit within a period of four weeks thereafter.
8. Copies of both the affidavits shall be made over to Mr. Shivansh,
learned  advocate  who  is  assisting  Mr.  Rishi  Malhotra,  learned  amicus
curiae. 
Chandigarh
9. O.A. Nos.1034 & 1329 of 2023, preferred by the applicants in I.A.
No.164964/2026 are left free to pursue their remedy before the Central
Administrative Tribunal, Chandigarh Bench (CAT).
10. The CAT shall proceed to decide the claims and entitlements of the
applicants  before  it  for  appointment  on  the  23  posts  which,  learned
counsel for the UT Administration informs us, are reserved for contractual
teachers. 
14

--- Page 23 ---
11. We place on record the submission of the learned counsel for the UT
Administration  that  16  of  the  23  contractual  teachers,  who  had
participated in the written examination conducted by such Administration,
failed to qualify in such examination.
12. The  effect  of  the  applicants  not  being  able  to  succeed  in  the
qualifying examination is left open for consideration by the CAT, should a
challenge  be  laid  in  accordance  with  law.  I.A.  No.164964/2026  for
intervention is, accordingly, disposed of.   
13. Mr. Malhotra, learned amicus curiae pointing to the affidavit filed by
UT Administration on 16 th July, 2025 submits that substantial progress has
been made for appointment of special teachers.
14. Out of 96 posts which were advertised, 36 posts have been filled up.
It  is  also  submitted  that 23  posts  have  been reserved for  contractual
teachers; also that, 21 RCI qualified candidates appeared in the written
examination but were not found qualified in such test.
15. Be that as it may, having regard to the submission made by learned
counsel for the UT Administration that appointments have been made and
further appointments are in the pipeline, we grant such administration
further four weeks’ time to place on record an updated status report with
regard to such appointments. 
Himachal Pradesh
16. Mr. Anil Nag, learned counsel appearing for the State of Himachal
Pradesh, submits that 245 posts of special teachers have been created
(138 from pre-primary to Class V and 107 from Class VI to Class XII) and
15

--- Page 24 ---
that recruitment process is in progress and, in fact, the examination has
been conducted yesterday.
17. Mr. Nag also submits that within a period of six weeks from date, the
State would be in a position to make regular appointments.
18. We require the State of Himachal Pradesh to file an updated status
report after the appointments are made, in pursuance of the examination
conducted yesterday within four weeks. 
19. In the updated status report to be filed in terms of the aforesaid
direction, the State of Himachal Pradesh shall also indicate the number of
contractual  teachers  screened by  the  Screening  Committee  which  has
been constituted vide notification dated 17 th April, 2025 and how many of
the screened teachers have been found suitable for appointment. 
Uttarakhand
20. Better affidavit be filed by the State of Uttarakhand by four weeks.
21. Issue notice on I.A. No.221639/2025.
22. Mr.  Ashutosh  Kumar  Sharma,  learned  counsel  accepts  notice  on
behalf of the State of Uttarakhand.
23. Counter affidavit I.A. No.221639/2025 be filed by three weeks.
24. We propose to take up the cases related to the States of Telangana,
Assam, Rajasthan, Chhattisgarh and Bihar on 28th July, 2026 at 03:00 p.m.
(RASHMI DHYANI PANT)                        (SUDHIR KUMAR SHARMA)

CORRECTED
IN THE SUPREME COURT OF INDIA
CIVIL APPELLATE JURISDICTION
CIVIL APPEAL NO.5182/2025
(@Petition for Special Leave to Appeal (C)  No.14061/2024)
PHOENIX ARC PRIVATE LIMITED                        Appellant(s)
                                VERSUS
M/S. SAMARPANA CHARITABLE TRUST & ORS.             Respondent(s)
 O R D E R
1. Leave granted
2. This appeal arises from an order passed by the High Court of
Judicature at Madras dated 18-3-2024 in CMP No.6040/2024 in OSA SR
No.8560/2024, by which the High Court rejected the application
filed by the appellant – herein and thereby declined to grant leave
to appeal against the Judgment and order passed by the learned
Single Judge dated 5-9-2022 in OP No.260/2022.
3. The OP No.260/2022 was instituted at the instance of M/s.
Samarpana Charitable Trust represented by its authorized person
(Respondent No.1 – herein).
4. We  take  notice  of  the  fact  that  the  proceedings  were
instituted only against M/s.Chennai Metro Rail Project – Respondent
No.2 – herein.
5. The operative part of the order passed by the High Court in OP
No.260/2022 reads thus:-
“Para 11 Therefore, in view of that particular aspect, the
permission which is required to sell property is hereby granted
and the parties may proceed further. Necessary sale deeds may be
executed in terms of this particular order and if required, this
Order  may  also  be  presented  before  the  Jurisdictional  Sub
Registrar at the time of registration.

--- Page 34 ---
2
Para 12 The remaining property described in Schedule A which
is in item Nos.2 & 3, after the property is sold to the respondent
should remain and must remain in the custody and control and
possession of the 1st petitioner/Trust.”
6. It is the case of the appellant - herein that in its absence,
the learned Single Judge could not have decided the OP No.260/2022.
7. In such circumstances, it went before the Division Bench of
the High Court and prayed for leave to appeal.
8. The leave to appeal came to be declined.
9. In such circumstances, the appellant is here before us with
the present appeal.
10. We  heard  Mr.  Ranjit  Kumar,  the  learned  Senior  counsel
appearing for the appellant, Mr. Anand Sanjay Nuli, the learned
Senior counsel appearing for Respondent No.1 – Trust and Mr. Mukul
Rohatgi, the learned Senior counsel appearing for Respondent No.2 -
M/s. Chennai Metro Rail Project.
11. We also take notice of the fact that M/s. Chennai Metro Rail
Project  has  preferred  an  application  seeking  to  implead  the
original borrowers.
12. As we are inclined to dispose of this appeal, it is not
necessary for us to implead the original borrowers.
13. We take notice of the order passed by a Co-ordinate Bench of
this Court dated 19-7-2024. The same reads thus:-
1.  Heard  Mr.  Ranjit  Kumar,  learned  senior  counsel
appearing for the petitioner(s).
2. The counsel would refer to the Settlement Deed dated
29.01.2021 to say that the two brothers – P.J.K. Sairam and
P.K.S. Prashath were the mortgagors for the loan, secured from
the Andhra Bank. The petitioner – Company is an assignee of the
loan under the Securitisation and Reconstruction of Financial
Assets  and  Enforcement  of  Security  Interest  Act,  2002.
Considering the nature 1 of the claim that the assignee had

--- Page 35 ---
3
vis-a-vis two mortgagors and the terms of the Settlement Deed
dated 29.01.2021, the Division Bench ought to have granted
leave  to  the  petitioner(s)  to  challenge  the  order  dated
05.09.2022 of the learned Single Judge. This is more so when
the petitioner(s) were not arrayed as party in the proceedings
before the learned Single Judge.
3. Issue notice, returnable in four weeks.
4. From the submission of the learned senior counsel, it
appears that there are 7 Suits pending between the parties.
Therefore, it is submitted that at this stage, the Trust should
not project itself as the owner of the property on the strength
of the  order passed by the learned Single Judge on 05.09.2022.
Accepting this, the operation of the order (dated 05.09.2022)
to this extent, is stayed as an interim measure.”
14. Without commenting anything on the merits or demerits of the
impugned order passed by the High Court, we are of the view that we
should grant leave to the appellant – herein to file appeal against
the order passed by the learned Single Judge in O.P. No.260/2022
dated 5.9.2022. We order accordingly.
15. The impugned order passed by the High Court is hereby set
aside.
16. As we have granted leave to appeal, the appeal shall now be
registered and the Appellate Court, i.e., the Division Bench shall
hear this appeal and decide the same in accordance with law within
a period of two months from today.
17. We request the High Court to adhere to this time limit of two
months having regard to a huge public project involved in the
litigation.
18. All that we say today is that the interim order which has been
passed by this Court dated 19-7-2024 shall continue till the time
the appeal of the appellant is decided by the Division Bench.
However, with clarification that this interim order shall not come

--- Page 36 ---
4
in the way of M/s. Chennai Metro Rail Project so far as their
project is concerned.
19. With the aforesaid, the appeal stands disposed of.
20. Pending applications, if any, shall also stand disposed of.

1
IN THE SUPREME COURT OF INDIA
CIVIL APPELLATE JURISDICTION
CIVIL APPEAL NO.        OF 2026
(Arising out of SLP (C) No. 27136 of 2023)
HANSA JAIN … APPELLANT
VERSUS
VINOD KUMAR SANGHAI (DECEASED) THR. 
LEGAL REPRESENTAIVES & ANR. … RESPONDENTS
O R D E R
1. Leave granted.
2. Being aggrieved by an ex parte granted on 12.10.2018, the
appellant had preferred an application under Order IX Rule 13
which was rejected vide order dated 06.01.2020. On filing a
civil revision, it was also dismissed vide order impugned on
06.10.2023.  Being dissatisfied by both these orders, the
present appeal has been filed.
3. On issuing notice, the landlord tendered appearance and
filed counter affidavit. On 28.11.2025, direction was issued
to file the details of the arrears and rent till date.
Thereafter on 05.12.2025, this Court passed an order in the
proceedings which is as under :

--- Page 73 ---
2
“1) Apropos previous order, the statement
of dues of rent has been filed by the
petitioner as well as the respondents.
2)  Learned  counsel  for  the  petitioner
contends  that  the  rent  is  due  from
November,  2021,  and  prior  to  the  said
period, rent has already been paid in the
account of Mr.Vinod Kumar Sanghai (since
deceased)  (husband  of  the  landlady).
Learned counsel appearing on behalf of the
respondents wishes to verify the said fact.
The bank account details produced along
with the special leave petition be verified
by the respondent who shall revert on the
same by filing an affidavit within four
weeks.
3) In the meantime, as per the calculation
placed before us by the respondent, a sum
of Rs.15,44,762/-is due up to December,
2025, adding escalated rent in terms of the
agreement.  The  petitioner  is  ready  to
deposit the said amount within the time as
directed by this Court. 
4) In view of the above, we postpone the
hearing of this case till 23.01.2026. The
petitioner  shall  deposit  a  sum  of
Rs.15,44,762/- with the Registry of this
Court  which  shall  be  kept  in  interest
bearing  short  term  fixed  deposit  of  a
nationalised Bank on auto renewal basis.
5) The respondent shall verify the bank
account statement and file an affidavit
ascertaining  about  the  deposit  and
informing if the deposit is not made by the
petitioner.
6) List on 23.01.2026.
7) Interim order to continue till then.”

--- Page 74 ---
3
4. Learned counsel for the appellant submits that they have
deposited the rent as directed till the end of May, 2026 which
is disclosed in the affidavit calculating Rs.16,000/- per
month adding 5% escalated rent every year.  The amount of Rs.
15,44,762 has been deposited on 22.01.2025 which is lying in
an interest bearing fixed deposit and the remaining rent from
January to May, 2026 of Rs.4,01,445/- has been deposited by
the appellant on 18.05.2026 and it is kept in a non-interest
bearing account.  As such the amount of the arrears of rent
till May, 2026 has been deposited subject to verification by
the landlord.
5. After hearing learned counsel for the parties at length
and considering the facts, wherein the ex parte was proceeded
within 33 days from the date of service and the judgment has
been pronounced immediately and within 32 days, as urged even
without lapse of the statutory period for filing the counter
affidavit  granting  decree  of  eviction,  in  our  view,  a
reasonable opportunity of hearing ought to be given to the
appellant to put his defence.  Therefore, we set aside the ex
parte decree and allow the application under Order IX, Rule 13
of Civil Procedure Code, 1908.
6. In consequence, the suit be restored to its file in its

--- Page 75 ---
4
original number.  The appellant undertakes to file Written
Statement on or before July 16, 2026 and on the said date both
parties shall appear before the trial court.  Thereafter the
suit be decided as expeditiously as possible not later than
one year.
7. The amount of rent deposited by the appellant shall be
transmitted in the account of Respondent No.2 on supply of the
details of the bank account along with the interest accrued
thereon.
8. With the above directions, the appeal stands allowed and
disposed of.  Pending applications, if any, shall stand
disposed of.

IN THE SUPREME COURT OF INDIA
CIVIL APPELLATE JURISDICTION
CIVIL APPEAL NO.         /2026
(@ SLP(C) No.  30538/2025)
BCIL ZED RIA PROPERTIES PVT. LTD. & ANR. APPELLANT(S)
          VERSUS
ARAVIND RESPONDENT(S)
O R D E R
1. Leave granted. 
2. M/s.  Aishu  Dreamland  Private  Limited,  the  Successful
Resolution Applicant 1, that took over and stepped into the
shoes of the Corporate Debtor, BCIL ZED RIA Properties Pvt.
Ltd., is aggrieved by the order dated 05.03.2025 passed by the
High Court of Judicature at Madras in Writ Petition No.
10749/2024. 
3. By the said order, the High Court confirmed the order dated
30.01.2024 passed by the National Consumer Disputes Resolution
Commission2, New Delhi, in First Appeal No. 591/2023, refusing
to condone delay of 105 days in the filing of the said appeal
by the SRA against the order dated 11.10.2022 passed by the
Tamil Nadu State Consumer Disputes Redressal Commission 3 in
Complaint No. 16/2019. 
1  For short “SRA”
2  For short “NCDRC”
3  For short “SCDRC”
1

--- Page 79 ---
4. A few crucial facts may be noted for the effective disposal of
this appeal. 
5. Corporate Insolvency Resolution Process against the Corporate
Debtor, BCIL ZED RIA Properties Pvt. Ltd, was initiated on
09.08.2018.  In effect, the moratorium under Section 14 of the
Insolvency and Bankruptcy Code, 2016 4, started operating from
the said date.
6. In terms of the said statutory provision, it was not open to
any litigant to initiate fresh litigation or continue with
pending litigation against the Corporate Debtor, BCIL ZED RIA
Properties Pvt. Ltd. While so, the respondent approached the
SCDRC only on 04.12.2018 with his consumer complaint against
the Corporate Debtor in relation to his Sale and Construction
Agreement dated 25.01.2016. 
7. Unmindful of the statutory scheme of the IBC, the SCDRC passed
ex parte order dated 11.10.2022, allowing the complaint case
filed by the respondent, and directed the Corporate Debtor to
refund certain amounts along with interest and costs. 
8. Upon finding out about the passing of the said order, the SRA
of the Corporate Debtor filed an appeal before the NCDRC along
with an application to condone the delay of 105 days in
preferring the said appeal. This application came to be
dismissed by the NCDRC and was, thereafter, confirmed by the
High Court, vide the impugned order.
9. Given the aforestated facts, it is clear that the very filing
of the consumer complaint against the Corporate Debtor was hit
4  For short “IBC”
2

--- Page 80 ---
by the moratorium order and the SRA, therefore, had an
arguable case to raise before the NCDRC.  The delay on its
part was also not substantial and given the fact that the
order passed by the SCDRC was an ex parte one, the NCDRC ought
to have been more liberal in considering the condone delay
application.
10. The appeal is, accordingly, allowed, setting aside the orders
passed by the High Court as well as the NCDRC.  The delay of
105 days in the filing of First Appeal No. 591/2023 is
condoned.  The said appeal shall stand restored to the file of
the NCDRC and the same shall be considered on merits and in
accordance with law expeditiously.
11. Pending application(s), if any, shall stand disposed of. 
..........................J.
(SANJAY KUMAR)
..........................J.
(K. VINOD CHANDRAN)
NEW DELHI;
MAY 18, 2026.
3

--- Page 81 ---

CRIMINAL APPEAL NO. __           _____ OF 2026 
(@Special Leave Petition (Crl.) 36 of 2025) 
 
 
 
ASHA L. @ ASHA

O R D E R  
 
SANJAY KAROL, J. 
 
Leave Granted. 
 
2.   This appeal at the instance of the appellant-accused 
questions the correctness of judgment dated 11th September 2024 
passed by the High Court of Karnataka at Bengaluru, in Criminal 
Appeal no.199 of 2024 (A) which set aside the judgment passed 
Digitally signed by
SOURAV PAL
Date: 2026.06.04
16:08:48 IST
Reason:
Signature Not Verified

--- Page 94 ---
Crl.App.No..of 2026 @ SLP(Crl)No. 36 of 2025                                  Page 2 of 4 
 
in Crl. A. No.25319 of 2022 on the file of LXXII Additional City 
Civil and Sessions Judge at Mayo Hall, Bengaluru, which in turn 
had set aside the judgment in CC No.51657 of 2019 by XXXIII, 
Additional Chief Metropolitan Magistrate, Mayo Hall Unit, 
Bengaluru.  
3.  The appellant-accused had entered into an agreement with 
the complainant to buy the latter’s ongoing business concern , 
‘Purple Tree’, a salon, initially for a consideration of Rs. 68 lakhs 
and later at Rs.56 lakhs . It is undisputed that out of this, an 
amount Rs.27 lakhs stood paid. In furtherance of the remaining 
consideration amount, two cheques bearing nos.073776 for Rs.10 
lakhs and 073776 for Rs.9 lakhs were given to the complaina nt. 
When two of these cheques were presented for encashment, the 
same were dishonoured on account of payment having been 
stopped. Accordingly, a complaint dated 4 th October 2018 was 
lodged with the police. Although efforts were made to settle th e 
matter before the police authorities by way of payment worth 
Rs.5,50,000/- towards final consideration, it is alleged that  the 
same was not paid. The legal notice initiating proceedings wa s 
sent on 27 th November 2018 and reply thereto was filed on 5 th 
December 2018.  
The Trial Court convicted the appellant-accused and 
directed him to pay a sum of Rs.21,50,000/-. The First Appellate 

--- Page 95 ---
Crl.App.No..of 2026 @ SLP(Crl)No. 36 of 2025                                  Page 3 of 4 
 
Court acquitted, and the High Court again convicted the 
appellant-accused. Hence the matter stands before us.     
Heard learned counsel, senior counsel for the parties. 
4.  Given that the dispute inter se the parties arose from an 
Agreement to Sell,  and especially in view of the fact that parties 
have had a relationship of employer-employee between them for 
at least some time before disputes came to be, we had sent the 
matter to  Supreme Court Mediation Centre, in terms of order 
dated 13th January 2026. Despite best efforts, the matter could not 
be resolved and as such we asked the parties to be present on the 
next date of hearing. Pursuant to our interaction, certain event s 
took place which have been recorded in the additional affida vit 
dated 11th May 2026 filed by the respondent. One of the primary 
points therein was to transfer the leasehold rights of the property 
wherein the salon was located to the appellant-accused who had 
already taken over the operations of the entity. The landlord one 
Mr. S. Naga, apparently informed the respondent that the 
appellant-accused owing to financial difficulties have been 
unable to pay rent on the premises since April 2021 and as such  
had handed over the peaceful and vacant possession of the 
property to the landlord and also agreed specifically that he could 
sell all materials contained within the premises in an effort to  
realise the deficit in rent. This was done in terms of Agreement 
dated 22nd October 2021.  

--- Page 96 ---
Crl.App.No..of 2026 @ SLP(Crl)No. 36 of 2025                                  Page 4 of 4 
 
5.  In these circumstances, although the appellant-accused 
finally got the business, it did not fructify into a profitable 
business concern in her hands and at the end nothing remains. In 
these peculiar facts, convicting the appellant-accused in terms as 
decided by the Trial Court would be a fruitless exercise for an 
amount worth Rs.21,50,000/- would be unattainable, more so in  
view of the appellant accused’s defence set up in his response to 
the legal notice of the amount not being a debt due. The sentence 
is as such set aside. 
Appeal is allowed. Pending applications stand disposed of.

(SANJAY KAROL)

1. Delay condoned.
1

--- Page 99 ---
M.A.Diary No. 24243/2026
2. The petitioner before us is a convict.  He is undergoing
life imprisonment past more than 25 years. He wants this Court
to look into the order passed by this Court dated 24.04.2024 in
Criminal  Appeal  No.  1056  of  2015  titled  “Harbhajan  Singh
Versus  Intelligence  Officer,  Directorate  Of  Revenue
Intelligence”. The order reads thus:-
“1. By a concurrent judgment, the appellant has been
convicted for the offences punishable under Sections 21,
23  and  29  of  the  Narcotic  Drugs  &  Psychotropic
Substances, Act, 1985 (for short "the NDPS Act') apart
from Section 489-B, 489-C of the Indian Penal Code, 1860,
Section 25 of the Arms Act, 1959 and Sections 4 & 5 of
Explosive Substances Act, 1908. Accordingly, sentence
have been imposed for a period of twenty years for
certain offences while life imprisonment has been imposed
for the offence committed under Section 489-B of the
Indian Penal Code, 1860 (for short “the IPC”) and under
Section 4 and 5 of the Explosive Substances Act, 1908.
The High Court confirmed the order of conviction and
sentence passed by the Trial Court making it clear that
sentences shall run consecutively.
2.Though, learned counsel appearing for the appellant
made arguments on merit, we are not inclined to interfere
with  the judgment  of the  High Court  who took  into
consideration all the relevant materials while confirming
the conviction order passed by the Trial Court. 
3.The only other issue for consideration is with respect
to the sentence imposed. For considering the alternative
submission made, we directed the respondent-State to file
2

--- Page 100 ---
M.A.Diary No. 24243/2026
an affidavit on the conduct of the appellant during the
period of incarceration. The appellant has undergone
about a period of 21 years 07 months and 22 days of
actual sentence. The following is the relevant paragraphs
of the affidavit filed on behalf of the respondent:-
“5. That as per information received from
the Jail, the convict has undergone total of
21 years 07 months and 22 days of actual
sentence.
6. That as per information received from
the  Jail,  pertaining  to  the  attending
circumstances, particularly to the conduct of
convict, it is submitted that:
a) The above said convict has been
performing his prison duty which is
assigned to him by prison officials
satisfactory.
b) No case related to prison offence
has been registered against him and
convict  has  never  engaged  in  any
illegal activity inside the prison.
c) The above said convict has availed
total 07 paroles till date and no
adverse  report  during  his  stay  on
parole has ever been received in the
office of Superintendent Central Jail,
Amritsar.
7. That the answering respondent is bound
to  follow  the  directions  passed  by  this
Hon’ble Court in the present Appeal. A copy of
letter No.1644 dated 12.4.2024 received from
the  Superintendent,  Central  Jail,  Amritsar,
Punjab is Annexure A.”
4.We are inclined to take these averments, for coming to
the conclusion that they can be construed as mitigating
circumstances  to  facilitate  modifying  the  sentence
3

--- Page 101 ---
M.A.Diary No. 24243/2026
imposed. The conduct of the appellant during the period
of incarceration has been found to be satisfactory. The
occurrence took place way back in the year 2000. He was
also on parole on seven occasions. There was no adverse
report whenever the appellant was sent on parole. Thus,
making the appellant as a reformed person to get back
into the society, will not cause any problem. 
5.Thus in the light of the aforesaid factual position,
we  are  in clined  to  confirm  the  conviction  while
modifying the sentence passed under aforesaid sections
to one undergone i.e.  21 years 07 months and 22 days of
actual sentence. 
6.We have been informed that there are two more co-
accused similarly placed like that of the appellant. We
believe that the benefit conferred on the appellant will
have to be extended to them provided the report of the
jail authorities is satisfactory as in the case of the
appellant. In such view of the matter, we are inclined to
direct the respondents to give a copy of the order passed
by this Court to the co- accused who can approach this
Court for appropriate direction seeking the same relief
as being rendered to the appellant. 
7.In the event of inability of the co-accused persons to
have legal assistance of their own choice, a request
shall be made to the concerned legal aid Authority of
the State.  
8.The appeal is allowed in part. The appellant shall be
released forthwith, unless required in any other case.
Pending application(s), if any, shall stand disposed

concerned High Court Legal Services Authority.”
3. In view of the aforesaid, we direct the respondent-State to
file an affidavit on the conduct of the petitioner before us
during the period of 25 years of incarceration before the next
date of hearing.

O R D E R
1. Leave granted.
2. Heard learned counsel for the parties.
3. This appeal arises from an order dated 28.03.2025
passed by the Madras High Court, whereby the interim order
dated 30.09.2022 passed by the High Court in Appeal Suit
(A.S.)  No.433  of  2022,  staying  dispossession  of  the
appellant pending consideration of his appeal, has been
vacated. 
4. The submission on behalf of the appellant is that
first appeal is a valuable remedy where the court can deal
with both questions of fact and law, therefore, if the
interim protection granted is vacated, the purpose of the
1

--- Page 104 ---
appeal itself would stand frustrated. 
5. On 13.05.2025 following order was passed:
“Issue notice, returnable within four weeks.
Subject to deposit of Rs.5,00,000/- by the  
petitioner in the Registry of this Court within four 
weeks from today, the effect and operation of the 
impugned order dated 28.3.2025 passed by the High  
Court shall remain stayed.”
6. The learned counsel for the appellant submits that in
compliance of the order dated 13.05.2025, the appellant has
already deposited Rupees Five Lakhs in the Registry of this
Court.
7. Ordinarily where the order under appeal has serious
consequences, a stay of the order pending consideration of
appeal is appropriate, otherwise the remedy of appeal might
be rendered nugatory 1. However, the appellate court can
always impose conditions for the stay to protect the
interest  of  non-appellant.  As  the  appellant  here  has
deposited rupees 5 lacs, we deem it appropriate to set
aside the impugned order and dispose of this appeal by
directing that the interim order of the High Court dated
1 1 Mool Chand Yadav & another v. Raza Buland Sugar Company Ltd., Rampur 
& others, (1982) 3 SCC 484. 
2

--- Page 105 ---
30.09.2022 shall continue during pendency of appeal A.S.
No.433 of 2022 before the High Court. The amount deposited
by the appellant in the Registry of this Court along with
interest, if any, shall be remitted to the High Court. The
High Court shall invest the same in an interest-bearing
deposit of a nationalized bank, which shall abide the
decision of the appeal. We also request the High Court to
ensure that the appeal is decided expeditiously preferably
within a period of six months.
8. Appeal is disposed of in the above terms.
9. Pending application(s), if any, shall stand disposed
of.

IN THE SUPREME COURT OF INDIA 
CRIMINAL APPELLATE JURISDICTION 
CRIMINAL APPEAL NO. 2217 OF 2026
SURENDRA @ SUNDA APPELLANT(S)
 VERSUS 
THE STATE OF UTTAR PRADESH RESPONDENT(S)
O R D E R
1. The facts of this case are elaborated in the judgment dated
13.04.2026 rendered by a two-Judge Bench of this Court (J.K.
Maheshwari and Atul S. Chadurkar, JJ.). 1 The two-Judge Bench,
having realised the need for an automated uniform module governing
the premature release of life convicts, which ought to be given
effect to on pan-India basis through a software, that may be
developed  by  the  National  Informatics  Centre  (NIC),  issued
comprehensive directions that are contained in paragraph 22 of that
judgment. 
2. In furtherance thereto, and in collaboration with all relevant
stakeholders, software known as “E-Prisons Early Release Processing
Module” has now been launched by the NIC. 
3. With the responsibility having now been assigned to the State
Legal  Services  Authority,  in  collaboration  with  the  prisons
department  and  other  prescribed  authorities  of  the  State
Government, we deem it appropriate to pass a formal order of
closure  of  proceedings  in  the  instant  case.  The  appeal  is,
accordingly, disposed of.
4. However, before parting with this appeal, we would like to
1  2026 INSC 414.
1

--- Page 126 ---
formally  appreciate  and  acknowledge  the  outstanding  services
rendered by Mr. K. Parameshwar, learned senior counsel/Amicus
Curiae assisted by Mr. Ravi Raghunath, learned counsel, whose
initiative prompted the NIC to take up the aforementioned software
as a pilot project in Central Jail, Agra and District Jail, Lucknow
and further enabled the NIC to launch the software on a pan-India
basis.
5. Pending application(s), if any, shall stand closed.

ITEM NO.34               COURT NO.4               SECTION XV
               S U P R E M E  C O U R T  O F  I N D I A
                       RECORD OF PROCEEDINGS
Petition for Special Leave to Appeal (C) No.18887/2026
[Arising out of impugned final judgment and order dated 23-02-2026
in DBSAW No.209/2024 passed by the High Court of Judicature for
Rajasthan at Jaipur]
SURJI BAI                                          Petitioner
VERSUS
STATE OF RAJASTHAN & ORS.                          Respondents
FOR ADMISSION 
I.A. No.164813/2026-EXEMPTION FROM FILING O.T.
 
Date : 03-06-2026 This matter was called on for hearing today.
CORAM :  HON'BLE MR. JUSTICE DIPANKAR DATTA
         HON'BLE MR. JUSTICE SATISH CHANDRA SHARMA
PARTIAL COURT WORKING DAYS BENCH
For Petitioner(s) : Mr. Ajay Choudhary, AOR
                   
For Respondent(s) : 
          UPON hearing the counsel the Court made the following
                             O R D E R
1. One of the members of this Bench is inclined to issue notice on the ground
that the petitioner (despite being a pensioner herself, having served the Nagar
Palika, Lakheri for 34 years and retired in 2014) is entitled to family pension
arising out of death-in-harness in 1988 of her husband 1, having regard to the
provisions contained in the Rajasthan Service Rules, 1951.
2. The other member of this Bench is not inclined to issue notice in view of
Rules  10  and 13  of the  Rajasthan Municipal  Service  (Pension)  Rules, 1989,
because the petitioner’s husband passed away in 1988 without putting in the
qualifying service of 10 years.
1 who was also an employee of the same Nagar Palika
1

--- Page 180 ---
3. However, both members are ad idem that this difference of opinion would
necessarily lead to reference of this special leave petition to a 3-Judge Bench
and, in such event, the proceedings which relate to claim of family pension by
the petitioner could be protracted unnecessarily.  
4. At the same time, keeping in line with the age-old tradition of this Court
that notice ought to issue when both members of a Bench are divided in their
opinion, issuance of notice is also an available option.
5. In such view of the matter and to facilitate early disposal of the special
leave petition, it is proposed to issue notice with the observation that subject to
the order of the Hon’ble the Chief Justice of India, this special leave petition may
be placed before a different co-ordinate Bench for decision.
6. Ordered accordingly.
    (MANIK KUMAR)                           (SUDHIR KUMAR SHARMA)
SENIOR PERSONAL ASSISTANT                     COURT MASTER (NSH)
2

--- Page 181 ---

We are not inclined to entertain this petition
for grant of bail. The Special Leave Petition is,
accordingly, dismissed.
However,  considering  the  fact  that  the
petitioner has been in custody for about 3 years and 9
1

--- Page 280 ---
months and the fact that only charges have been framed,
we direct the Trial Court to make an endevour to
conclude the same within a period of one year from
today.
It goes without saying that the petitioner will
extend all cooperation in the conclusion of the trial.
In the event the trial is not concluded within
the aforesaid period, for no fault attributable to the
petitioner, it would be open for the petitioner to
revive his prayer for bail.
Pending application(s) shall stand disposed of.

agreement to contend that there is no arbitration agreement
between the parties.
2. Having considered the matter in detail, we are of the
opinion that the issue relating to the existence of an
arbitration  agreement  can  be  considered  by  the  Arbitral
Tribunal under Section 16 of the Act. In this view of the
matter, we permit the petitioner to raise all questions of law
and facts including those relating to the existence of an
arbitration agreement. The Arbitral Tribunal shall consider
the questions on its own merits without being influenced by
any observations made by the High Court disposing of the
Section 11 application.
3. With these observations, the Special Leave Petitions
stand disposed of.

disposed of.

                             O R D E R
1. The petitioner challenges the judgment and order dated
08.04.2026 in A.B.A. No.1442 of 2026, titled “ Satpal Singh
@ Soni Vs. The State of Jharkhand ”, passed by the High
Court of Jharkhand at Ranchi.
2. We have heard learned counsel for the petitioner.
3. Issue notice, returnable on 14.07.2026.
4. Mr. Vishnu Sharma, learned counsel, accepts notice on
behalf of the respondent/State of Jharkhand. Hence, the
formal service of notice on the respondent/State is waived.
1

--- Page 346 ---
5. The petitioner to serve a copy of the present petition
to learned counsel for the respondent/State forthwith.
6. Let counter affidavit be filed within three (03) weeks.
Rejoinder affidavit thereto, if any, be filed before the
next date of listing.
7. We make it clear that no further opportunity will be
granted for this purpose.
8. In the event of arrest in connection with FIR No.107 of
2023, Police Station – Telco, Jamshedpur, Jharkhand, the
petitioner shall be released on bail on the appropriate
terms and conditions as may be fixed by the Investigating
Officer/Arresting Officer. However, in the attending facts,
one of the conditions shall necessarily be that if the
petitioner  possesses  a  passport,  the  same  shall  be
deposited before the Competent Authority/Court, till the
conclusion of the Trial or directed otherwise.
9. The petitioner shall make himself available before the
Investigating Officer on 12.06.2026 at 10:00 a.m. and on
all such dates as he may be required.
10. Needless to add, till the investigation is not complete
in all respects, the petitioner would fully cooperate, and
if the challan/charge sheet is filed, he would maintain
good conduct and not attempt to influence any of the
witnesses in any manner till the completion of the trial.

                             O R D E R
1. Learned counsel appearing for the petitioner submits that the award of
the relevant Motor Accidents Claims Tribunal granting compensation has been
implemented by the insurer - respondent no.2 1 and that the petitioners have
since received the amount assessed as compensation.  However, the petitioners
are aggrieved because the High Court, by the impugned order, has condoned
the huge delay in presentation of the appeal under Section 173(1) of the Motor
Vehicles Act, 1988 by the owner – respondent no.1 2 against such award despite
1 insurer2 owner

--- Page 372 ---
2
the same being made in his presence.
2. It  is  submitted  on  behalf  of  the  petitioners  that  since  the  owner
approached the High Court at a point of time when the insurer was proceeding
against  him  in  execution  for  recovering  the  compensation  paid  to  the
petitioners  in  terms  of  the  award,  which  directed  the  insurer  to  ‘pay  and
recover’, the appeal before the High Court may be confined to the question as
to liability and not quantum.  
3. Issue notice, why this Court shall not direct that the owner shall not be
permitted to raise any question as to the quantum of compensation before the
High Court; instead, his appeal should be confined to the limited point that it is
the insurer who has to bear the liability for payment of such compensation and
such liability cannot be foisted on him.
